# Semantic Fact Layer

`SZrSemanticContext` 是编译期语义事实的唯一共享容器。parser、type inference、semantic analyzer 负责把表达式类型、引用、数值、可达性、逻辑和所有权事实写入这里；LSP 已开始查询这些事实，Debug 和 REPL 已开始接入同一诊断/表达式方向，完整事实复用仍在后续推进，避免各自复制一套局部推断规则。

## Stage 1 Reaching-Definition Payload

`SZrSemanticReferenceFact` carries two reaching-definition payload shapes. `definitionRange` / `hasDefinitionRange` remains the single-definition fast path used by `DefinitionOf` and older consumers. `definitionRanges` is a context-owned `SZrArray` of `SZrFileRange` values used when CFG-backed reaching definitions can enumerate multiple declaration/write locations reaching the same read. `ZrParser_SemanticFacts_Reset` / `Free` release this nested array for each reference fact before clearing the top-level fact array.

`ZrParser_SemanticFacts_ResolveLinearReachingDefinitions` continues to annotate straight-line reads with the latest preceding declaration/write. `ZrParser_SemanticFacts_ResolveControlFlowReachingDefinitions` now also preserves bounded multi-definition alternatives at ambiguous joins, including divergent branch writes and cloned `finally` paths. `ZrParser_SemanticQuery_DefinitionOf` still returns one best location, while `ZrParser_SemanticQuery_DefinitionsOf` returns all known matching declaration/write facts for multi-location consumers such as LSP go-to-definition.

## Stage 1 Definite Assignment Payload

`SZrSemanticReferenceFact` now also carries an optional definite-assignment state for reference facts. The payload is `hasDefiniteAssignmentState` plus `definiteAssignmentState`, with values `UNKNOWN`, `UNINIT`, `INIT`, and `MAYBE_INIT`. `semantic_query` consumes read states for diagnostics: `UNINIT` maps to `uninitialized_read`, while `MAYBE_INIT` maps to `possibly_uninitialized_read`.

`ZrParser_SemanticFacts_ResolveLinearDefiniteAssignments` is the first fact producer for this payload. It walks existing reference facts in order, treats explicitly marked declaration facts as the initial symbol state, treats write facts as `INIT`, and annotates reads with the latest known state for the same resolved symbol. Identifier write reference facts produced by type inference also pre-fill `INIT` so downstream consumers can observe the write state before a resolver pass. Unknown declarations leave reads as `UNKNOWN` / no-state so diagnostics do not invent errors.

`ZrParser_SemanticFacts_ResolveControlFlowDefiniteAssignments` is the first CFG-backed producer. It builds a symbol map from resolved declaration/read/write facts, initializes unassigned declarations as `UNINIT`, runs forward dataflow over script, function, test, and nested function-like CFG roots, and writes the joined state back to source read facts. Compiler assignment lowering now records identifier write facts for assignment targets instead of treating the left-hand side as a read, so a branch such as `if (flag) { seed = 1; } return seed;` produces a `MAYBE_INIT` read and a `possibly_uninitialized_read` semantic query diagnostic. Constant-true `while`/traditional `for` loops and omitted-condition `for(;;)` loops do not add a fake zero-iteration path in CFG, so a write followed by `break` can leave the subsequent read as `INIT` and suppress the false uninitialized-read diagnostic.

Numeric branch refinement now lives in `type_inference_branch_refinement.c` with focused parser/LSP branch tests. The branch scope supports simple identifier-vs-integer-literal comparisons on true and false branches, true-branch `&&` intersection, false-branch `||` complement intersection, true-branch equality, edge-only single-interval complements for representable `!=` true branches and `==` false branches, false-branch `!=` inversion to exact equality, representable same-direction subsets of true-branch `||` unions and false-branch `&&` complement unions, unary logical-not branch polarity inversion over those supported forms, `else if` scope stacking, and a fixed two-segment payload for tested same-identifier `||`/`&&` combinations. `SZrInferredType` and `SZrSemanticNumericFact` keep the existing min/max envelope while optionally carrying `rangeSegmentCount` / `rangeSegments`, so older consumers still see a conservative interval and semantic query consumers can inspect the precise split. `ZrParser_SemanticFacts_FindNumericByNode` prefers richer same-node numeric facts, so LSP symbol surfaces do not stop at an earlier broad initializer fact when a later branch-aware segmented fact exists for the same AST node. For example, `if (!(seed < 10)) { seed + 1; }` with `seed: 0..255` delegates to the false branch of `seed < 10`, so the parser-owned numeric fact and LSP local semantic query both report `11..256` for `seed + 1`. `if (seed < 10 || seed < 20) { seed + 1; }` narrows then-scope `seed` to `0..19` and reports `1..20`; `if (seed < 10 && seed < 20) { ... } else { seed + 1; }` narrows else-scope `seed` to `10..255` and reports `11..256`. `if (seed < 10 || seed > 20) { seed + 1; }` keeps then-scope `seed` as envelope `0..255` plus segments `0..9` / `21..255`, and the scalar addition path reports `seed + 1` as envelope `1..256` plus segments `1..10` / `22..256`; the false branch of `if (seed > 10 && seed < 20) { ... } else { seed + 1; }` similarly reports envelope `1..256` plus segments `1..11` / `21..256`. Nested same-identifier combinations can now first refine child conditions before merging: `if ((seed > 2 && seed < 10) || seed == 20) { seed + 1; }` reports envelope `4..21` plus segments `4..10` / `21..21`, and `else if (seed < 20) { seed + 1; }` after an outer `if (seed < 10)` false branch reports `11..20`. LSP local query, plain hover, public hover, rich hover, inlay hint labels, completion detail, and signature parameter documentation consume the same parser-owned segmented numeric fact for the fixed two-segment case. Interior true-branch inequality hole sets, arbitrary segment counts beyond the fixed payload, full hole-set modeling, arbitrary boolean formulas beyond the tested same-identifier subset, complete De Morgan expansion, CFG pruning, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain out of scope for this branch-refinement layer.

The segment payload is no longer limited to the two inline `rangeSegments` slots. `SZrInferredType` and `SZrSemanticNumericFact` keep the first two `SZrNumericRangeSegment` values inline and store additional segments in `rangeExtraSegments`; `type_system_numeric_segments.c` owns the shared reset/free/copy/append/access helpers so semantic facts, branch scopes, numeric `+`/`-` segment shifting, and LSP formatters do not duplicate storage rules. Current tested coverage proves true-branch interior `!=` hole splitting (`seed != 10` over `0..20` becomes `1..10` and `12..21` after `+ 1`) and same-identifier true-branch `||` three-segment output (`seed < 5 || seed == 10 || seed > 20` becomes `1..5`, `11..11`, and `22..256` after `+ 1`). A six-segment equality-disjunction fixture now verifies the internal fact keeps all segments after scalar `+ 1`, while `lsp_numeric_range_text.c` applies the editor-display cap from `ZR_LSP_NUMERIC_RANGE_SEGMENT_DISPLAY_LIMIT`: LSP hover/rich hover, inlay, completion, and signature docs render the first four segments and append `... +N more` for the hidden tail. `lsp_local_semantic_hover_text.c` now owns fact-to-hover text assembly so `lsp_local_semantic_query.c` stays focused on selection and materialization. This is a bounded representation and tested subset, not a claim of arbitrary symbolic boolean formulas, cross-block numeric dataflow, or unbounded segment growth.

`type_inference_branch_assignment_join.c` is the first narrow cross-block numeric assignment join. It is deliberately smaller than the planned CFG-wide numeric dataflow engine: parser `ZR_AST_IF_EXPRESSION` inference and LSP typecheck call it only for simple numeric assignment expressions in simple branch blocks. The original form supports an `if/else` whose then and else blocks each assign the same identifier and joins both right-hand-side ranges into one min/max envelope, so `if (flag) { narrowed = 1; } else { narrowed = 10; } narrowed + 1` produces `2..11` in parser facts and LSP local semantic query. The helper also supports one-sided assignment joins for the tested simple shapes: no-`else` true-branch assignment joins the true RHS range with the retained false-path pre-branch binding, while explicit else-only assignment joins the else RHS range with the retained true-path pre-branch binding. The tested multi-statement expansion is intentionally narrow: branch blocks may contain ordinary expression statements before or after simple assignment candidates, so both `if (flag) { flag; narrowed = 1; } else { flag; narrowed = 10; } narrowed + 1` and `if (flag) { narrowed = 1; flag; } else { narrowed = 10; flag; } narrowed + 1` produce `2..11`. The helper replays same-target sequential simple assignments in a branch-scoped temporary type environment, so RHS expressions can depend on earlier writes in the same branch without publishing those replay bindings as declaration facts; `if (flag) { narrowed = 1; narrowed = narrowed + 1; } else { narrowed = 10; narrowed = narrowed + 1; } narrowed + 1` produces `3..12`. The next bounded expansion records all simple assignment targets seen in both branch blocks, replays each branch in order, and joins each target's final reachable range back into the current environment. That lets cross-target RHS dependencies flow inside one branch block: `if (flag) { low = 1; high = low + 1; } else { low = 10; high = low + 10; } high + low` produces `3..30`. Unsupported assignment expressions still make the helper decline this shortcut instead of pretending to solve general branch dataflow. To make annotated locals participate in retained paths, `ZrParser_TypeInference_TryApplyInitializerNumericRange` preserves a compatible numeric initializer's single-point range on an explicitly annotated binding in both parser lambda-return analysis and LSP typecheck binding registration. For example, `var narrowed: int = 5; if (flag) { narrowed = 10; } return narrowed + 1;` and `var narrowed: int = 5; if (flag) { flag; } else { narrowed = 10; } return narrowed + 1;` both produce `6..11`. The current bounded nested expansion lets branch replay call the same helper for nested simple `if/else` blocks before the outer branch result is joined, so `if (flag) { if (inner) { narrowed = 1; } else { narrowed = 2; } } else { if (inner) { narrowed = 10; } else { narrowed = 20; } } narrowed + 1` produces `2..21`. This still does not model loops, arbitrary nested control-flow beyond simple nested if/else assignment blocks, unsupported assignment expressions, symbolic fixed points, or general reaching numeric definitions.

2026-06-23 update: segment-preserving assignment joins are now covered for this narrow branch-assignment shortcut. `type_inference_branch_assignment_segments.c` converts each branch result's single interval or existing segment payload into a local segment list, sorts and merges overlapping or adjacent segments, and writes a multi-segment payload back only when the joined result remains disjoint. The simple two-sided assignment fixture above now keeps envelope `2..11` plus segments `2..2` and `11..11` through the following `+ 1` expression in both parser facts and LSP local semantic query. After the later nested-assignment slice, the remaining limitation is narrower: loops, arbitrary nested control-flow beyond simple nested if/else assignment blocks, unsupported assignments, arbitrary symbolic range-set/hole-set reasoning beyond current segment-array operations, symbolic fixed points, and general reaching numeric definitions are still future work.

2026-06-23 update: nested simple if/else assignment replay is now covered for this narrow branch-assignment shortcut. Plan analysis recursively records simple assignment targets found inside nested `ZR_AST_IF_EXPRESSION` nodes, and branch replay first joins the nested if in the temporary branch scope before storing the current planned target bindings back into the outer branch result. The nested fixture with true-side writes `1`/`2` and false-side writes `10`/`20` now reports `2..21` after the following `+ 1` expression in both parser facts and LSP local semantic query. This is still a bounded replay shortcut, not a loop/fixed-point engine, not arbitrary nested CFG dataflow, and not a general reaching numeric-definition solver.

2026-06-23 update: unknown-condition while assignment zero-or-more range join is now covered as a separate narrow helper in `type_inference_loop_assignment_join.c`. Parser `ZR_AST_WHILE_LOOP` inference and LSP while typecheck call it after the loop condition/body traversal, and it joins the pre-loop binding with the single supported loop-body integer RHS so `var narrowed: int = 5; while (flag) { narrowed = 10; } return narrowed + 1;` reports `6..11`. The helper deliberately declines constant-condition loops, blocks with more than one assignment or other statements, self-dependent RHS, for/foreach, multi-target loops, fixed points, unsupported assignment expressions, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow.

2026-06-23 update: unknown-condition while multi-target assignment replay is now covered by the same focused loop helper. The helper plans all simple assignments in order, replays the loop body in a temporary type environment, allows later RHS expressions to read earlier loop-body target writes, then joins each replayed target range with its pre-loop range. `low=5, high=20; while (flag) { low = 1; high = low + 10; } high + low;` now reports `12..25` in both parser facts and LSP local semantic query. To avoid unsound fixed-point inference, RHS expressions still cannot read a planned target before it has been assigned in the replay; self-dependent RHS, for/foreach, unsupported statements/assignments, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: unknown-condition while multi-statement assignment replay now tolerates ordinary expression statements around simple numeric assignments. `type_inference_loop_assignment_join.c` collects only assignment expressions into its replay plan and ignores expression statements such as `flag;`, so `narrowed=5; while (flag) { flag; narrowed = 10; flag; } narrowed + 1;` reports `6..11` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. Non-expression statements, nested control flow inside the loop body, unsupported assignment expressions, self-dependent RHS, for/foreach, true loop fixed points, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain out of scope.

2026-06-23 update: unknown-condition while nested-if assignment replay now handles a bounded nested simple `if/else` as a loop replay step. The loop helper collects nested assignment targets, replays the nested branch through the existing `ZrParser_TypeInference_TryJoinIfElseNumericAssignments` inside the temporary loop replay scope, stores current plan target bindings, then performs the same outer zero-or-more pre-loop/loop-body join. `narrowed=5; while (flag) { if (inner) { narrowed = 1; } else { narrowed = 10; } } narrowed + 1;` reports `2..11` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. This does not claim nested loops, self-dependent RHS, for/foreach, true loop fixed points, unsupported statements/assignments, or general CFG-wide numeric dataflow.

2026-06-23 update: unknown-condition while self-dependent increment replay now handles the first bounded self-dependent RHS shape without claiming a full loop fixed point. `type_inference_loop_assignment_self_dependency.c` recognizes `target = target + positive_integer_literal` only when that target has not already been assigned earlier in the current loop replay plan. During replay, it computes the one-or-more iteration result from the source binding as `[preMin + delta, INT64_MAX]`, clears stale segment payloads, and lets the existing loop join combine that widened loop-body range with the retained pre-loop range. Thus `narrowed=5; while (flag) { narrowed = narrowed + 1; } narrowed + 0;` reports `5..9223372036854775807` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. Self-decrement, non-literal deltas, multiplicative or conditional recurrences, later RHS expressions that lose range due to the `INT64_MAX` boundary, nested loops, for/foreach, true fixed points, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: unknown-condition while self-dependent decrement replay extends the same narrow helper to signed deltas. `type_inference_loop_assignment_self_dependency.c` now recognizes `target = target - positive_integer_literal` for a first write to that target in the loop replay plan, stores a negative delta, and widens the one-or-more iteration result to `[INT64_MIN, preMax - literal]` before the existing zero-or-more join with the pre-loop binding. Thus `narrowed=5; while (flag) { narrowed = narrowed - 1; } narrowed + 0;` reports `-9223372036854775808..5` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. Because that range crosses below zero, the LSP assignment query test helper now requires unsigned numeric payloads only for expected non-negative intervals. Non-literal deltas, `literal - target`, multiplicative or conditional recurrences, boundary cases where one iteration would overflow, nested loops, for/foreach, true fixed points, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: unknown-condition while self-dependent positive singleton identifier deltas are now covered for the same bounded widening shortcut. `type_inference_loop_assignment_self_dependency.c` still accepts positive integer literals, and now also accepts a non-target identifier when the current type environment proves that identifier is an int64 singleton positive range. The loop plan validator rejects the shortcut if that delta identifier is one of the planned loop assignment targets, so a value written inside the same replay cannot be treated as stable. Thus `narrowed=5; step=1; while (flag) { narrowed = narrowed + step; } narrowed + 0;` reports `5..9223372036854775807` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. Non-singleton identifiers, identifiers written by the same loop, non-identifier complex deltas, negative identifier deltas, multiplicative or conditional recurrences, nested loops, for/foreach, true fixed points, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: unknown-condition while self-dependent positive-range identifier deltas are now covered by the same conservative widening shortcut. `type_inference_loop_assignment_self_dependency.c` accepts a non-target identifier when the current type environment proves that identifier is an int64 range with a strictly positive lower bound, using that lower bound as the minimum one-iteration delta and widening the upper endpoint to `INT64_MAX`. The same validator still rejects delta identifiers written by the replay plan. Thus `narrowed=5; step=1..3; while (flag) { narrowed = narrowed + step; } narrowed + 0;` reports `5..9223372036854775807` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. Delta ranges that may include zero or negative values, complex delta expressions, multiplicative or conditional recurrences, nested loops, for/foreach, true fixed points, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: unknown-condition while self-dependent positive expression deltas are now covered for the same bounded widening shortcut. `type_inference_loop_assignment_self_dependency.c` extracts the delta operand from `target + delta`, `delta + target`, or `target - delta`, rejects expressions that reference the target or use unsupported member/call shapes, and then asks the existing expression inference path for an int64 range with a strictly positive lower bound. `type_inference_loop_assignment_join.c` now validates the whole delta expression against the loop replay plan's target set, so an expression that reads any value written by the same bounded replay plan cannot be treated as a stable recurrence step. Thus `narrowed=5; step=1..3; while (flag) { narrowed = narrowed + (step + 1); } narrowed + 0;` reports `5..9223372036854775807` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. Delta expressions that may evaluate to zero or negative values, same-loop-written dependencies, member/call/unsupported expression shapes, multiplicative or conditional recurrences, nested loops, for/foreach, true fixed points, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: unknown-condition while self-dependent zero-inclusive positive-possible deltas are now covered by the same bounded recurrence shortcut. The loop plan stores signed delta min/max instead of a single strict-positive lower bound, and the self-dependency helper accepts supported int64 delta expressions whose inferred range has `min >= 0` and `max > 0` while still rejecting target reads, same replay-plan target dependencies, and unsupported member/call shapes. `target + delta` widens the one-or-more result to `[preMin + deltaMin, INT64_MAX]`, so a zero-inclusive delta keeps the original lower endpoint after the zero-or-more join; `target - delta` records the corresponding signed negative range for lower-bound widening. Thus `narrowed=5; step=0..3; while (flag) { narrowed = narrowed + step; } narrowed + 0;` reports `5..9223372036854775807` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. Zero-only no-op deltas, negative or sign-crossing delta expressions, same-loop-written dependencies, member/call/unsupported expression shapes, multiplicative or conditional recurrences, nested loops, for/foreach, true fixed points, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: unknown-condition while self-dependent zero-inclusive negative-possible deltas are now covered by the same signed delta-range shortcut. The self-dependency helper now accepts supported int64 delta expressions whose inferred range has `min < 0` and `max <= 0`, in addition to the already accepted nonnegative positive-possible range. During replay, the negative signed range widens the one-or-more result to `[INT64_MIN, preMax + deltaMax]`; with a zero-inclusive upper bound, the existing zero-or-more join keeps the original upper endpoint. Thus `narrowed=5; step=-3..0; while (flag) { narrowed = narrowed + step; } narrowed + 0;` reports `-9223372036854775808..5` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. Zero-only no-op deltas, sign-crossing delta expressions, same-loop-written dependencies, member/call/unsupported expression shapes, multiplicative or conditional recurrences, nested loops, for/foreach, true fixed points, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: unknown-condition while self-dependent sign-crossing stable deltas are now covered by the same signed delta-range shortcut. The self-dependency helper accepts supported int64 delta expressions whose inferred range has `min < 0` and `max > 0`; because the stable loop input can be negative in some executions and positive in others, the conservative zero-or-more result must include both decreasing and increasing recurrence envelopes. The replay therefore widens directly to `[INT64_MIN, INT64_MAX]` before publishing the joined binding. Thus `narrowed=5; step=-3..3; while (flag) { narrowed = narrowed + step; } narrowed + 0;` reports `-9223372036854775808..9223372036854775807` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. Zero-only no-op deltas, same-loop-written dependencies, member/call/unsupported expression shapes, multiplicative or conditional recurrences, nested loops, for/foreach, true fixed points, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: unknown-condition while self-dependent direct identifier deltas written earlier in the same loop body are now covered for a narrow stable replay shape. `type_inference_loop_assignment_join.c` marks first-write `target = target + deltaIdentifier` assignments for replay-time delta resolution when the delta identifier is assigned by an earlier supported step in the same replay plan. During replay, the earlier assignment first stores its numeric binding in the temporary loop scope, then the self-dependency helper resolves the delta range from that scope and applies the existing signed widening logic. Thus `narrowed=5; step=0; while (flag) { step = 2; narrowed = narrowed + step; } narrowed + 0;` reports `5..9223372036854775807` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. This only claims direct identifier deltas from earlier supported same-loop assignments in the tested positive singleton shape; zero-only no-op deltas, broader same-loop dependency chains, member/call/unsupported expression shapes, multiplicative or conditional recurrences, nested loops, for/foreach, true fixed points, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: unknown-condition while self-dependent delta expressions can now depend on earlier supported writes in the same loop replay plan. The join helper checks deferred self-dependent candidates before trying to treat the delta as stable in the pre-loop scope: it extracts the delta expression, confirms it reads at least one loop target, requires every loop-target read in that expression to be assigned before the current self-dependent step, and then lets replay resolve the expression from the temporary loop scope. Thus `narrowed=5; step=0; while (flag) { step = 2; narrowed = narrowed + (step + 1); } narrowed + 0;` reports `5..9223372036854775807` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. This only claims supported same-loop-written delta expressions whose loop-target dependencies are earlier in replay order; zero-only no-op deltas, chained or multiple same-loop delta writes, member/call/unsupported expression shapes, multiplicative or conditional recurrences, nested loops, for/foreach, true fixed points, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: unknown-condition while self-dependent zero-only deltas are now accepted as no-op replay steps. The self-dependency helper accepts `0..0` signed delta ranges, and `WidenSelfDependentType` copies the source type unchanged for that shape instead of widening or failing the loop plan. Thus `narrowed=5; other=0; while (flag) { narrowed = narrowed + 0; other = 10; } other + 0;` reports `0..10` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. This only claims first-write zero-only no-op deltas that preserve bounded replay; chained/multiple same-loop deltas beyond preserving no-op prefixes, member/call/unsupported expression shapes, multiplicative or conditional recurrences, nested loops, for/foreach, true fixed points, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-24 update: unknown-condition while self-dependent replay now treats earlier same-target zero-only no-op writes as preserving prefixes for a later self-dependent delta. The loop assignment plan distinguishes a prior target write that changes the replay value from a prior `0..0` self-dependent no-op; if every prior same-target write before the current step is such a no-op and no nested step assigns the target, the later assignment can still use self-dependent signed-delta widening. Thus `narrowed=5; while (flag) { narrowed = narrowed + 0; narrowed = narrowed + 1; } narrowed + 0;` reports `5..9223372036854775807` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query instead of the previous `5..6` one-iteration replay envelope. To keep the loop join helper below the large-file threshold, replay result storage and step execution moved to `type_inference_loop_assignment_replay.c`, leaving `type_inference_loop_assignment_join.c` focused on plan collection, validation, and final zero-or-more joining. This only claims zero-only preserving prefixes followed by a positive self-dependent delta; arbitrary same-target multi-write recurrences, non-no-op prefixes, member/call/unsupported expression shapes, multiplicative or conditional recurrences, true fixed points, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-24 update: unknown-condition while self-dependent replay now groups adjacent same-target stable self-dependent steps before widening. Plan collection allows a step to extend the immediately previous same-target stable self-dependent step, and replay sums the sequence's signed delta ranges before applying one self-dependent widen from the pre-sequence source binding. Thus `narrowed=5; while (flag) { narrowed = narrowed + 1; narrowed = narrowed - 1; } narrowed + 0;` reports `5..5` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query instead of first widening after `+1` and then replaying `-1` over `5..9223372036854775807`. This only claims adjacent same-target stable self-dependent sequences such as the tested net-zero `+1`/`-1` case; non-adjacent or interleaved multi-write recurrence, variable-correlation refinement, member/call/unsupported expression shapes, multiplicative or conditional recurrences, true fixed points, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-24 update: unknown-condition while self-dependent replay now allows target-independent ordinary assignments between same-target stable self-dependent steps. Plan collection scans backward through assignment steps that do not write the sequence target, do not read that target in their RHS, and are not self-dependent/deferred replay steps; replay executes those interleaved assignments while accumulating the same-target signed delta sequence. Thus `narrowed=5; other=0; while (flag) { narrowed = narrowed + 1; other = 10; narrowed = narrowed - 1; } narrowed + 0;` reports `5..5` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query instead of the previous `5..9223372036854775806`. This only claims target-independent ordinary assignment interleaves; interleaves that read the sequence target, non-zero multi-write recurrence precision, variable-correlation refinement, member/call/unsupported expression shapes, multiplicative or conditional recurrences, true fixed points, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-24 update: unknown-condition while self-dependent replay now accepts a narrow target-reading interleave shape when the whole same-target sequence is exactly net-zero. Plan collection may cross an ordinary assignment whose RHS reads the sequence target only after proving the earlier stable same-target delta plus the current stable delta sums to `0..0`; replay then pre-scans the sequence, temporarily binds the target to `source range + accumulated delta` before replaying the target-reading assignment, and finally commits the net-zero target type. Thus `narrowed=5; other=0; while (flag) { narrowed = narrowed + 1; other = narrowed; narrowed = narrowed - 1; } narrowed + 0; other + 0;` reports `narrowed` as `5..5` and `other` as `0..6` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. This only claims exact net-zero target-reading ordinary assignment interleaves; target-reading non-zero recurrence precision, variable-correlation generalization, member/call/unsupported expression shapes, multiplicative or conditional recurrences, true fixed points, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-24 update: unknown-condition while self-dependent replay now accepts the tested target-reading interleaved net-negative sequence. Plan collection may cross an ordinary assignment whose RHS reads the sequence target when the earlier stable same-target delta plus the current stable delta still forms a supported self-dependent recurrence delta; replay stores the reader's temporary target binding as the envelope of first-iteration `source range + accumulated delta` and later-iteration `widen(source, totalDelta) + accumulated delta`. Thus `narrowed=5; other=0; while (flag) { narrowed = narrowed + 1; other = narrowed; narrowed = narrowed - 2; } narrowed + 0; other + 0;` reports `narrowed` as `-9223372036854775808..5` and `other` as `-9223372036854775808..6` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. TDD first failed the WSL gcc parser fixture with `Expected -9223372036854775808 Was 4`, and implementation validation also exposed an LSP query offset / numeric fact kind helper boundary before the final green run. WSL gcc, WSL clang, and Windows MSVC focused verification then passed parser 12 PASS, LSP 12 PASS/checks, adjacent loop assignment 16 PASS, and adjacent LSP branch-assignment 25 PASS/checks. This only claims the ordinary target-reading interleave shape for the tested net-negative stable same-target sequence; target-reading positive/sign-crossing fixtures, variable-correlation generalization, member/call/unsupported expression shapes, multiplicative or conditional recurrences, true fixed points, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-24 update: unknown-condition while self-dependent replay now accepts a same-target sequence whose later delta must be resolved from an earlier same-loop assignment. Plan collection can extend an existing same-target stable self-dependent sequence with a replay-resolved self-dependent step when that step's delta expression depends only on earlier supported replay assignments and no interleaved assignment reads the sequence target. During replay, the ordinary `step = 2` assignment runs first, the later `narrowed = narrowed + step` resolves its delta from the temporary loop scope, and the sequence widens once from the original source using the combined `+1` then `+step` delta. Thus `narrowed=5; step=0; while (flag) { step = 2; narrowed = narrowed + 1; narrowed = narrowed + step; } narrowed + 0;` reports `5..9223372036854775807` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. This only claims same-target stable-prefix plus replay-resolved same-loop-written delta sequences without target-reading interleaves; target-reading interleaves combined with replay-resolved deltas, chained or multiple same-loop delta dependencies, member/call/unsupported expression shapes, multiplicative or conditional recurrences, true fixed points, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-24 update: unknown-condition while self-dependent replay now accepts multiple adjacent same-target replay-resolved same-loop-written delta steps when each delta depends only on earlier supported replay assignments. Plan collection treats an earlier same-target replay-resolved step as a valid sequence prefix for the next replay-resolved same-target step, while still rejecting target-reading interleaves and unrelated deferred/self-dependent steps. During replay, both `narrowed = narrowed + step` writes resolve `step` from the temporary loop scope after `step = 2`, and the accumulated signed delta widens from the original source. Thus `narrowed=5; step=0; while (flag) { step = 2; narrowed = narrowed + step; narrowed = narrowed + step; } narrowed + 0;` reports `5..9223372036854775807` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. This narrows the earlier multiple same-loop-written limitation to more complex chained dependencies, target-reading with replay-resolved deltas, member/call/unsupported expression shapes, multiplicative or conditional recurrences, true fixed points, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow.

2026-06-24 update: unknown-condition while self-dependent replay now accepts the exact-net-zero shape where a target-reading interleave sits between replay-resolved deltas. Plan collection can let a replay-resolved same-target sequence cross an ordinary assignment whose RHS reads the sequence target, but replay must first resolve the full sequence from the temporary loop scope and only enables that reader when the total delta is exactly `0..0`. During replay, `step = 1` executes before the sequence, both `narrowed = narrowed + step` and `narrowed = narrowed - step` resolve their delta from that scope, and `other = narrowed` reads the intermediate `source + accumulated delta`. Thus `narrowed=5; other=0; step=0; while (flag) { step = 1; narrowed = narrowed + step; other = narrowed; narrowed = narrowed - step; } narrowed + 0; other + 0;` reports `narrowed` as `5..5` and `other` as `0..6` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. TDD first failed the WSL gcc parser fixture with `Expected 5 Was 9223372036854775806`, and the paired LSP query returned target `5..9223372036854775806` plus observer `0..9223372036854775807`. WSL gcc, WSL clang, and Windows MSVC focused verification then passed parser 15 PASS, LSP 15 PASS/checks, adjacent loop assignment 16 PASS, and adjacent LSP branch-assignment 25 PASS/checks. This only claims earlier supported replay assignments feeding an exact-net-zero replay-resolved same-target sequence with one ordinary target-reading interleave; replay-resolved non-zero/sign-crossing target-reading recurrence, member/call/unsupported delta expressions, unsupported assignments, true fixed points, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-24 update: unknown-condition while self-dependent replay now preserves the tested symbolic net-zero shape where a target-reading interleave sits between opposite stable direct identifier deltas. Replay tracks a single direct delta identifier and its signed balance while scanning same-target stable self-dependent steps, so `narrowed = narrowed + step; other = narrowed; narrowed = narrowed - step` can submit a full sequence delta of `0..0` even when `step` itself has a sign-crossing range. The reader still observes the prefix delta: `narrowed=5; other=0; step=-3..3; while (flag) { narrowed = narrowed + step; other = narrowed; narrowed = narrowed - step; } narrowed + 0; other + 0;` reports `narrowed` as `5..5` and `other` as `0..8` through parser facts; the LSP fixture with `step = seed - 128` reports `narrowed=5..5` and `other=-123..132`. This only claims direct identifier deltas whose same symbol cancels exactly and whose dependency is not rewritten by an intervening ordinary assignment; non-cancelling target-reading sign-crossing/positive recurrences, replay-resolved positive/sign-crossing target-reading shapes, member/call/unsupported delta expressions, unsupported assignments, true fixed points, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-24 update: unknown-condition while self-dependent replay now extends symbolic net-zero target-reading replay from direct identifiers to structurally identical supported delta expressions. Sequence pre-scan, delta accumulation, target-reading interleave allowance, and intermediate reader storage now live in `type_inference_loop_assignment_sequence.c/.h`, keeping `type_inference_loop_assignment_replay.c` focused on replay execution and reducing it from 987 lines to 456. The symbolic tracker stores the extracted delta AST and compares later deltas with conservative structural equality over supported literals, identifiers, unary/binary/logical/conditional/type-cast, and memberless primary expressions; it does not algebraically normalize distinct shapes. Thus `narrowed=5; other=0; step=-3..3; while (flag) { narrowed = narrowed + (step + 1); other = narrowed; narrowed = narrowed - (step + 1); } narrowed + 0; other + 0;` reports `narrowed` as `5..5` and `other` as `0..9` through parser facts; the LSP fixture with `step = seed - 128` reports `narrowed=5..5` and `other=-122..133`. This only claims same-shape supported delta expression cancellation; commuted/algebraically equivalent expressions, member/call/unsupported delta expressions, target-reading positive/sign-crossing non-cancelling recurrence, fixed points, and general CFG-wide loop dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-24 update: unknown-condition while self-dependent replay now accepts the tested commuted binary-plus symbolic net-zero target-reading shape. The delta expression equality path first checks same-operator structural equality and then, only for binary `+`, retries with left/right operands swapped. Thus `narrowed=5; other=0; step=-3..3; while (flag) { narrowed = narrowed + (step + 1); other = narrowed; narrowed = narrowed - (1 + step); } narrowed + 0; other + 0;` still reports `narrowed` as `5..5` and `other` as `0..9` through parser facts; the LSP fixture with `step = seed - 128` reports `narrowed=5..5` and `other=-122..133`. This only claims commuted exact-zero matching for supported binary `+` delta expressions; subtraction/multiplication normalization, constant-folded expression equivalence, member/call/unsupported delta expressions, non-cancelling target-reading recurrence, fixed points, and general CFG-wide loop dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-24 update: unknown-condition while self-dependent replay now accepts the tested net-negative shape where a target-reading interleave sits between replay-resolved deltas. Replay sequence pre-scan resolves `narrowed = narrowed + step` and `narrowed = narrowed - (step + 1)` from the temporary loop scope after the earlier `step = 1` assignment, and allows the reader when the full replay-resolved sequence delta is supported net-negative. Before allowing that path, pre-scan also rejects ordinary interleaves that would write a dependency read by a later replay-resolved delta. Thus `narrowed=5; other=0; step=0; while (flag) { step = 1; narrowed = narrowed + step; other = narrowed; narrowed = narrowed - (step + 1); } narrowed + 0; other + 0;` reports `narrowed` as `-9223372036854775808..5` and `other` as `-9223372036854775808..6` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. TDD first failed the WSL gcc parser fixture with `Expected 5 Was 9223372036854775805`, and the paired LSP query returned target `-9223372036854775808..9223372036854775805` plus observer `0..9223372036854775807`. WSL gcc, WSL clang, and Windows MSVC focused verification then passed parser 16 PASS, LSP 16 PASS/checks, adjacent loop assignment 16 PASS, and adjacent LSP branch-assignment 25 PASS/checks. This only claims earlier supported replay assignments feeding a net-negative replay-resolved same-target sequence with one ordinary target-reading interleave and no prior interleave write to delta dependencies; replay-resolved positive/sign-crossing target-reading recurrence, member/call/unsupported delta expressions, unsupported assignments, true fixed points, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: init-free/no-step traditional `for` assignment replay now reuses the bounded loop helper without widening its claim to general loop dataflow. `ZrParser_TypeInference_TryJoinForNumericAssignments` accepts only `ZR_AST_FOR_LOOP` nodes with no init, an explicit unknown condition, and no step, then calls the same loop-body replay/join body used by unknown-condition `while`. Parser for-expression inference and LSP for typecheck both call the helper, so `narrowed=5; for (; flag; ) { narrowed = 10; } narrowed + 1;` reports `6..11` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. Loop assignment parser coverage moved to `test_numeric_loop_assignment_dataflow.c`, which now owns the existing while loop assignment cases plus the new traditional for case. For variable-declaration init, step dataflow, omitted or constant for conditions, foreach, nested loop bodies, non-literal recurrences, true fixed points, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: `foreach` assignment replay now uses the same bounded zero-or-more loop join for body assignments that do not depend on the foreach item. `type_inference_loop_assignment_entry.c` owns the public while/for/foreach entry wrappers and condition filtering, while `type_inference_loop_assignment_join.c` exposes the shared body join through `type_inference_loop_assignment_join_internal.h`. Parser `ZR_AST_FOREACH_LOOP` inference and LSP foreach typecheck both call `ZrParser_TypeInference_TryJoinForeachNumericAssignments`, so `narrowed=5; foreach (item in items) { narrowed = 10; } narrowed + 1;` reports `6..11` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query when `items` is an unknown-length array. This only claims a zero-or-more join for supported body assignment replay; item-dependent RHS, iterable cardinality refinement, for variable-declaration init/step/constant-condition forms, nested loop bodies, non-literal recurrences, true fixed points, unsupported statements/assignments, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: direct `foreach` item-dependent assignment replay is now covered for the same bounded zero-or-more loop helper. The foreach entry helper infers the iterable expression, binds the direct identifier item from the iterable element type in a temporary replay scope, runs the existing loop body join while that item binding is visible, and commits only numeric assignment targets back to the outer environment so the item binding does not leak. With an `items` element range of `2..4`, `narrowed=5; foreach (item in items) { narrowed = item; } narrowed + 1;` now reports `3..6` through parser facts; the LSP `items: u8[]` fixture reports `1..256`. This remains a direct-identifier, element-range replay shortcut: destructuring patterns, explicit foreach type annotation-only inference, iterable cardinality refinement, nested loop bodies, true fixed points, unsupported statements/assignments, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: `foreach` assignment replay now distinguishes statically nonempty arrays from unknown-length arrays. The foreach entry helper keeps the existing direct identifier item binding path, records whether the inferred iterable array type has a nonempty size constraint (`arrayMinSize > 0` or `arrayFixedSize > 0`), and dispatches to `ZrParser_TypeInferenceLoopAssignment_JoinBodyAtLeastOnce` when at least one iteration is guaranteed. The shared loop join helper can now run a plan with or without the pre-loop path; the default `JoinBody` still includes zero iterations, while the new at-least-once entry joins the loop replay result against itself so the old binding is not retained. Thus `items: int[2]` with `narrowed=5; foreach (item in items) { narrowed = 10; } narrowed + 1` reports `11..11`, while unknown-length `int[]` still reports `6..11`. This remains limited to array size constraints and bounded assignment replay; dynamic nonemptiness proofs, non-array iterables, destructuring patterns, true fixed points, unsupported statements/assignments, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: traditional `for` assignment init is now covered for the no-step, explicit unknown-condition shape. `type_inference_loop_assignment_entry.c` applies only supported assignment-expression init nodes in a temporary type environment, reusing public assignment inference and `ZrParser_TypeInference_TryApplyInitializerNumericRange` so the target binding keeps symbol/type/declaration metadata while adopting the init RHS range. The helper then runs the existing loop-body replay/join from that init-updated scope and commits the temporary binding back to the saved outer environment only after both init and loop-body join succeed. Thus `narrowed=5; for (narrowed = 1; flag; ) { narrowed = 10; } narrowed + 1;` reports `2..11` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query: zero iterations see the init result `1`, while one or more iterations see the body result `10`. This is still a bounded shortcut, not full `for` dataflow; variable-declaration init, step effects, omitted/constant conditions, nested loops, item-dependent foreach RHS, non-literal recurrences, true fixed points, unsupported statements/assignments, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: traditional `for` assignment step is now covered for the no-init, explicit unknown-condition shape. `ZrParser_TypeInferenceLoopAssignment_JoinBodyWithStep` collects a supported loop body, appends the assignment step as the final replay step, and then performs the same zero-or-more pre-loop/body replay join. That means the zero-iteration path keeps the entering binding while the one-or-more path observes body execution followed by the step assignment. Thus `narrowed=5; for (; flag; narrowed = 10) { flag; } narrowed + 1;` reports `6..11` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. The current-scope binding writer moved to `type_inference_loop_assignment_scope.c`, keeping the main loop join helper below 1000 lines. This still only claims assignment-expression steps with existing numeric-range targets and numeric-range RHS under an explicit unknown condition; variable-declaration init, combined init+step coverage, omitted/constant conditions, nested loops, item-dependent foreach RHS, non-literal recurrences, true fixed points, unsupported statements/assignments, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: direct identifier `var` init in a traditional `for` header is now covered for the same explicit unknown-condition loop replay shortcut. `type_inference_loop_assignment_entry.c` recognizes `ZR_AST_VARIABLE_DECLARATION` init nodes with a direct identifier pattern and an inferable numeric initializer, registers that binding in the temporary for-init replay scope, then lets the existing body/step replay read it. When the joined scope is committed back to the saved outer environment, the helper skips the loop-local init name so the header variable does not leak. Thus `narrowed=5; for (var step: int = 10; flag; ) { narrowed = step; } narrowed + 1;` reports `6..11` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. This only claims direct identifier `var` declarations with initializer numeric ranges and current bounded assignment replay; destructuring declarations, declaration-without-initializer, non-range initializers, omitted or constant conditions, nested loops, true fixed points, unsupported statements/assignments, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: known-false traditional `for` assignment init now applies before the loop body is proven unreachable. `type_inference_loop_assignment_entry.c` checks the condition's exact boolean fact in `ZrParser_TypeInference_TryJoinForNumericAssignments`; when the condition is false, it applies only supported assignment-expression init nodes and deliberately skips body and step replay. Thus `narrowed=5; for (narrowed = 1; false; ) { narrowed = 10; } narrowed + 1;` reports `2..2` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. This remains a narrow shortcut: known-true or omitted conditions, known-false variable-declaration init leakage, combined init+step precision, nested loops, true fixed points, unsupported statements/assignments, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: non-assignment traditional `for` step expressions no longer suppress the existing bounded body assignment join. `type_inference_loop_assignment_entry.c` now routes assignment steps to `ZrParser_TypeInferenceLoopAssignment_JoinBodyWithStep`, but routes non-assignment step expressions such as `flag` back through the body-only zero-or-more join. Thus `narrowed=5; for (; flag; flag) { narrowed = 10; } narrowed + 1;` reports `6..11` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query, retaining the zero-iteration pre-loop path and the one-or-more body assignment path. This only claims non-assignment step expressions do not block bounded body replay; step side-effect precision, nested loops, true fixed points, unsupported non-expression statements, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: known-false traditional `for` assignment init now recognizes folded false conditions beyond the literal `false` token. `type_inference_loop_assignment_entry.c` checks bool literals first, then condition logical facts through `type_inference_logical_fact_known_bool_value`, and finally falls back to `type_inference_node_bool_value` for AST constant boolean expressions that may be available before the LSP analyzer has materialized the same logical fact. Thus `narrowed=5; for (narrowed = 1; 1 == 2; ) { narrowed = 10; } narrowed + 1;` reports `2..2` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. This remains a deterministic-false shortcut for supported assignment-expression init only: known-true or omitted conditions, false-condition variable-declaration init, combined init+step precision, nested loops, true fixed points, unsupported statements/assignments, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: traditional `for` combined assignment init + assignment step coverage is now captured in focused parser and LSP targets. No production code changed for this slice: the existing entry helper already applies the init in a temporary scope and passes that scope into the body+step replay path. Thus `narrowed=5; for (narrowed = 1; flag; narrowed = 10) { flag; } narrowed + 1;` reports `2..11` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query: zero iterations see the init result `1`, while one or more completed iterations see the step assignment `10`. This remains bounded replay coverage, not full `for` dataflow; known-true or omitted conditions, false-condition variable-declaration init, nested loops, true fixed points, step side-effect precision, unsupported statements/assignments, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: LSP traditional `for` typechecking now keeps variable-declaration init bindings scoped when the condition is known false. `semantic_analyzer_typecheck.c` pushes a runtime type-binding scope for `ZR_AST_FOR_LOOP` headers whose init is `ZR_AST_VARIABLE_DECLARATION`, typechecks init/condition/step/body while the header binding is visible, then pops before `ZrParser_TypeInference_TryJoinForNumericAssignments` publishes supported outer assignment facts. Parser type inference already kept the header binding scoped; new parser coverage locks that no-leak behavior. Thus `for (var step: int = 10; false; ) { narrowed = step; } step + 1` leaves the following expression without a numeric fact in both parser and LSP, while known-false assignment init still reports `2..2` and unknown-condition direct var-init body replay still reports `6..11`. This only claims direct `var` init scope isolation, not destructuring/no-range declarations, initializer side-effect dataflow, known-true/omitted conditions, dynamic loop fixed points, or general CFG-wide numeric dataflow.

2026-06-23 update: no-init/no-step traditional `for` with a known-true or omitted condition now has one bounded at-least-once break-prefix replay path. `ZrParser_TypeInference_TryJoinForNumericAssignments` routes `for (; true; )` and `for (;;)` forms with no init/step to `ZrParser_TypeInferenceLoopAssignment_JoinBodyAtLeastOnce`, and `type_inference_loop_assignment_join.c` treats a plain `break;` as the end of the replayable prefix. Thus `narrowed=5; for (; true; ) { narrowed = 10; break; } narrowed + 1;` and the omitted-condition variant both report `11..11` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. This only claims supported numeric assignment before a plain break in no-init/no-step loops; init/step/header-local binding variants, non-plain break/continue, nested or symbolic control flow, true fixed points, unsupported assignment expressions, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: known-true/omitted traditional `for` with a supported init and no step now extends that at-least-once break-prefix path. `type_inference_loop_assignment_entry.c` reuses the existing for-init temporary scope for supported assignment-expression init and direct identifier `var` init, then dispatches to `ZrParser_TypeInferenceLoopAssignment_JoinBodyAtLeastOnce` when the condition is known true or omitted and there is no step. The joined scope is committed back to the saved outer environment while still skipping a header-local init binding, so `for (var step: int = 10; true; ) { narrowed = step; break; } narrowed + 1;` can read `step` inside the loop without leaking it afterward. Assignment-init true/omitted fixtures and direct var-init true/omitted fixtures now report `11..11` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. This only claims no-step supported init/header-local break-prefix replay before a plain `break;`; step handling, combined var-init+step, destructuring/no-range header bindings, false-condition init side effects, non-plain break/continue, nested or symbolic control flow, true fixed points, unsupported assignment expressions, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: known-true/omitted traditional `for` with a step now has a bounded step-before-break path when there is no init. `ZrParser_TypeInferenceLoopAssignment_StatementIsPlainBreak` lives in the loop syntax helper module and is shared by the body-plan collector and the entry dispatcher. If a no-init `for` has a known-true or omitted condition, a step expression, and a top-level plain `break;` in the body, `type_inference_loop_assignment_entry.c` can prove that step is skipped on that first iteration exit path and routes the body prefix through `ZrParser_TypeInferenceLoopAssignment_JoinBodyAtLeastOnce`. Thus `for (; true; narrowed = 20) { narrowed = 10; break; } narrowed + 1;` and `for (;; narrowed = 20) { narrowed = 10; break; } narrowed + 1;` report `11..11` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query, not the pre-loop `6..6` or step result `21..21`. This only claims no-init, top-level plain-break-before-step, supported numeric body assignment; init+step/header-local+step, nested break, continue, break with expression, known-true loops without a break, fixed points, unsupported assignment expressions, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: known-true/omitted traditional `for` init+step and header-local+step forms now reuse the same step-before-break proof. `type_inference_loop_assignment_entry.c` applies supported assignment init or direct identifier `var` init in the existing temporary for-init scope, and then calls the at-least-once body replay even when a step exists if a top-level plain `break;` proves the step is skipped on the first-iteration exit path. Thus assignment-init+step true/omitted fixtures and direct var-init+step true/omitted fixtures report `11..11` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. This only claims supported init/header-local bindings plus step when a top-level plain `break;` exits before the step; nested break, continue, break with expression, known-true loops without a break, complex body control flow, fixed points, unsupported assignment expressions, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: the same step-before-break path now recognizes one bounded nested-if control-flow shape. `ZrParser_TypeInferenceLoopAssignment_StatementGuaranteesPlainBreak` in `type_inference_loop_assignment_syntax.c` proves that a top-level `if/else` statement skips the step when both then and else branches guarantee a plain `break;`. `type_inference_loop_assignment_entry.c` accepts that guarantee for known-true/omitted traditional `for` loops with a step, and the body plan collector records the nested-if assignment before stopping replay. Thus `for (; true; narrowed = 20) { if (flag) { narrowed = 10; break; } else { narrowed = 12; break; } } narrowed + 1;` reports `11..13` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query. This only claims top-level if/else with both branches ending in plain break and supported nested-if assignment replay; missing else, branch-without-break, continue, break with expression, known-true loops without a break, complex nested control flow, fixed points, unsupported assignment expressions, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

2026-06-23 update: the step-before-break path now also recognizes a deterministic true single-branch `if`. `type_inference_loop_assignment_entry.c` reuses the same literal/logical-fact/constant bool evaluator as loop condition handling to prove that a top-level `if (true)` enters only the then branch; `type_inference_loop_assignment_nested_if.c` treats a missing `else` as a no-assignment target path during target collection; and `type_inference_branch_assignment_join.c` commits only the reachable branch when an `if` condition is known. Thus `for (; true; narrowed = 20) { if (true) { narrowed = 10; break; } } narrowed + 1;` reports `11..11` through parser facts and LSP local semantic query, rather than retaining the pre-loop `6..6` path or the skipped step's `21..21` path. This only claims top-level deterministic-true `if` then-branch assignment plus plain break before the step; symbolic or unknown if conditions, unknown missing-else branches, branches without break, continue, break with expression, no-break known-true loops, complex nested control flow, fixed points, unsupported assignments, and general CFG-wide numeric dataflow remain future work.

Exact logical facts can now feed branch reachability diagnostics. `type_inference_logical_fact_known_bool_value` reads parser-owned `ALWAYS_TRUE` / `ALWAYS_FALSE` facts after interval comparison inference, so compiler conditional expressions like `seed < 300 ? 1 : 2` record constant-branch reachability and publish `unreachable_code` through semantic query diagnostics. LSP `if` analysis materializes condition facts before branch traversal and records the same constant branch reachability for `if (seed < 300) ... else ...`; LSP diagnostic de-duplication compares range and code so the direct `unreachable_branch` warning does not hide semantic query `unreachable_code`. This still only consumes exact logical facts; symbolic interval splitting, broader overflow analysis, and general CFG pruning remain future work.

Numeric overflow facts also feed semantic query diagnostics. `ZrParser_SemanticQuery_Diagnostics` maps any scoped numeric fact with `mayOverflow=true` to warning `numeric_overflow`, so existing type-inference facts for expressions like `9223372036854775807 + 1` are visible in parser query results, compiler `queryDiagnostics`, and LSP diagnostics. This is a diagnostic bridge over existing facts only; it does not add new overflow inference, symbolic arithmetic, or CFG-wide numeric dataflow.

Fixed-size and finite-max array bounds facts now feed semantic query diagnostics as well. Computed member inference for arrays first checks indexes that `type_inference_node_integer_value` can evaluate; negative indexes or constants at/above a known upper bound record a computed-member expression fact carrying a bounds diagnostic message. For non-constant index expressions, the same path infers the index expression type and uses its integer range: a whole range proven out of bounds maps to error `array_index_out_of_bounds`, such as `index: u8` in `values[index + 2]` for a two-element array, while a range that overlaps legal indexes but also contains invalid values maps to warning `array_index_may_be_out_of_bounds`, such as `values[index]` with `index: u8` and array size 2. Known non-integer index types now map to error `array_index_type_mismatch`; unknown/no-inferable index expressions and untyped object indexes remain silent to avoid false positives. Fixed-size array literals, `min==max` constraints, and finite `arrayMaxSize` constraints all provide an upper bound; primitive integer parameters such as `index: int` already receive their full type range during AST type conversion, so they also flow through the possible-warning path. Min-only / no finite-upper-bound arrays do not diagnose positive indexes as out of bounds, but they now warn when a known integer index range may be negative; that message omits the finite-size label because no upper bound exists. `SZrSemanticExpressionFact` carries optional `diagnosticCode` and `diagnosticSeverity` payloads, so `ZrParser_SemanticQuery_Diagnostics` can preserve exact error versus possible warning versus type-mismatch semantics instead of hard-coding every computed-member diagnostic as `array_index_out_of_bounds`. The array bounds/type diagnostic builders live in `type_inference_array_diagnostics.c` to keep the broader semantic-fact emission file from absorbing more bounds-specific responsibility. This bounds work still does not diagnose truly unknown/no-inferable-range indexes, and it does not add runtime bounds checks or CFG-wide numeric dataflow.

当前阶段建立容器和查询契约，并已开始从 type inference 写入表达式、数值、确定性逻辑和 ownership builtin 事实，从 LSP semantic analyzer 写入声明/使用引用事实、不可达事实、编辑器短路/分支逻辑事实和所有权违规事实。parser 也开始把代表性语法错误转换成结构化诊断，再通过 LSP 展示具体原因和建议。LSP 局部查询已接入表达式事实、数值事实、引用事实、诊断失败和显式 unknown 分流；hover/rich hover 现在也能把 expression kind/exactness/constant 和调用/成员 expression payload 作为 `Expression:` / escaped `Constant:` / `Call:` / `Member:` 行及稳定 role 暴露给编辑器，并能在 `seed[index]` 的 `[` 这类非 identifier 位置通过 member-access reference fact 恢复 computed member payload。Stdio inline values 也复用同一 local semantic query，覆盖 local initializer、简单 return、简单 line-start expression statement（包括 `!true;` / `-42;` 这类 unary 起始形式，`pick(42);` / `seed.value;` / `seed[index];` 这类 call/member 起始形式，以及 `[1 + 2];` / `[true || false];` 这类 array literal aggregate 起始形式、`{[1 + 2]: 4};`、`{a: 1 + 2};`、`{\n a: 1 + 2\n};` 这类 object aggregate 起始形式）、多行 return expression、return 后换行开始的 expression、等号后换行的 local initializer，以及 request range 从 continuation line 开始的简单 operator-split expression statement 的 fact-backed `InlineValueText`；`stdio_inline_value_scan.c/.h` 只定位 expression range 和 query token，事实仍由 `ZrLanguageServer_LspLocalSemanticQuery_ExpressionAt` 提供。当同一 query 返回 reference fact 时，inline value 会追加 `reference ...`，例如 computed member read 的 `reference member access`，array/object aggregate statement 则只显示共享 nested element/operator facts，例如 `range 3..3` 或 `logical true, short-circuits`。Debug 和 REPL 已开始以安全局部方式消费诊断和表达式能力；Debug 数据面在协议边界报告 value preview / evaluate result 的 named/indexed child shape，帮助 adapter 做局部展开判断，并且成功 `evaluate` 结果会通过 `debug_semantic_facts.c` 追加 parser/type-inference 已证明的 expression/numeric/logical/reachability facts、expression payloads 以及已有 reference facts，例如 computed member evaluate 会显示 `member index` / `reference member access index`，当前暂停帧里的 `inside + 1` 会在临时 type environment replay 后显示 parser-owned `reference read inside`，稳定 Debug global 如 `zr` 会显示 parser-owned `reference read zr`，编译入口函数的 top-level callable metadata 会注册进临时 type environment，所以 `pick(1 + 2)` 这类 Debug semantic-summary 查询可以追加 parser-owned `call pick args=1`、`reference call pick` 以及实参表达式的折叠事实。REPL 的 `:type <expression>` 已是第一个命令行事实消费者：它直接调用 parser/type inference，并能在同一 REPL 会话中复用 prior declaration 源码上下文来输出同一 `SZrSemanticContext` 里的数值/逻辑/所有权事实、调用/成员 expression payload、member-access reference facts 和 member-write reference facts。REPL 的普通裸表达式执行也接受完整的 aggregate-start 表达式，例如 `[1 + 2][0]` 会经内部 expression wrapping 执行并打印 `3`，`[1 + 2]` 会通过 shared array value stringification 打印 `[3]`；该路径依赖 parser/compiler/runtime 正常创建数组字面量和 `ZrCore_Value_ConvertToString` 正常展示数组，而不是走 `:type` 的 compile-time fact display。更完整的 Debug write/user-global/imported/generic-call reference parity、长期 REPL runtime cell 作用域和跨工具共享查询 parity 仍在后续任务中接入。

LSP declared-type prototype 会把 legacy `%unique T` 和泛型写法 `Unique<T>`、`Shared<T>`、`Weak<T>`、`Borrow<T>`、`Loan<T>` 归一化成 inner surface type 加 `ownershipQualifier`。所有权诊断先比较同一个 surface type，再比较 qualifier，因此 `%unique Resource` 与 `%shared Resource` 会以共同的 `Resource` surface 参与 mismatch/escape/weak-upgrade 分类；展示层也会在渲染签名、hover 和 completion detail 前拆掉 ownership wrapper，避免输出 `%unique Unique<Resource>` 这类双重限定。

Parser 语句分派现在也会在行首 `{...}` 遇到对象键形状时保留 expression-statement 语义：`{` 后若是 identifier/string key 加 `:`，或 computed key `[...]` 加 `:`，会按 object literal expression statement 解析，普通 block 仍走 block parser。LSP local semantic query 先按选中的 expression fact 节点查 numeric fact；若命中的是外层 object/array structural expression 且节点本身没有 numeric fact，则回退扫描同一 `SZrSemanticContext` 中包含 query range 的最窄 numeric fact。因此 stdio inline value 能在 `{[1 + 2]: 4};` 这类语句里显示 computed-key operator 的 `range 3..3` / `unsigned range 3..3`，而无需在 stdio 层复制 parser/type-inference 推断。

REPL 的普通裸表达式执行现在也覆盖行首对象字面量。`repl_input_scan.c` 会把空对象、标识符/字符串键后跟 `:`、或计算键 `[...]` 后跟 `:` 的 `{...}` 识别为对象表达式，所以 `{a: 1 + 2}.a` 和 `{[1 + 2]: 4}[3]` 会走和数组 aggregate-start 表达式相同的内部 `return <expr>;` 路径；普通 `{ var ... }` / `{ if ... }` 块仍留给 parser 语句路径。

Debug runtime snapshot 还会在协议层报告 `semanticSummary` / `referenceSummary`。`semanticSummary` 保留 runtime value preview 摘要，同时对成功的 `evaluate` 表达式追加 parser/type-inference 能证明的共享事实；例如 `evaluate("1 + 2")` 会在 `integer 3` 后追加 `expression binary exact`、`constant 3`、`range 3..3` 和 `unsigned range 3..3`，`evaluate("true || false")` 会追加 `short-circuits` 与 `unreachable because short-circuit skips evaluation`，`evaluate("true ? 1 : 2")` 会追加 constant-branch skipped-path reachability，字符串常量会按 REPL/LSP 相同规则转义 quote、backslash、`\n`、`\t`、`\r`、`\b`、`\f` 和其它控制字节，例如追加 `constant "a\"b\\c\n\t"` 形式的单行摘要，`evaluate("zr[1]")` 还会追加 parser-owned `reference member access`，`evaluate("inside + 1")` 会在暂停帧有可见 `inside` slot 时追加 parser-owned `reference read inside`，`evaluate("zr")` 会为稳定 Debug global 追加 parser-owned `reference read zr`。若 Debug agent 有编译入口函数，`debug_semantic_facts.c` 还会把该 entry function 的 top-level callable bindings、child function return type、parameter metadata 注册为临时 parser 函数签名；因此语义摘要查询 `pick(1 + 2)` 可以复用 parser/type inference 记录 `call pick args=1`、`reference call pick`、`expression binary exact`、`constant 3`、`range 3..3` 和 `unsigned range 3..3`，`seed[index]` 也可显示 `member index`、`reference member access index` 和索引 token 的 `reference read index`，但这仍不让 safe evaluator 执行函数调用或写入。 这条桥接由 `debug_semantic_facts.c` 负责：它把 evaluate 源码解析成临时表达式语句；若存在暂停帧，会先用可见 frame slots 的 runtime value type 填充临时 parser type environment，并注册稳定 Debug globals（`loadedModules`、`zr`、当前异常存在时的 `error`）和普通入口 callable metadata，再调用 `ZrParser_ExpressionType_Infer`，最后只格式化已有 `SZrSemanticExpressionFact` / `SZrSemanticNumericFact` / `SZrSemanticReferenceFact` / `SZrSemanticLogicalFact` / `SZrSemanticReachabilityFact` / `SZrSemanticOwnershipFact`；Debug safe evaluator 不复制类型推断、常量折叠、范围推断、引用分类、分支语义推断、调用/成员 payload 推断、unsigned range payload 推断或字符串常量转义策略。`referenceSummary` 现在能覆盖稳定顶层 scope 引用、简单 identifier evaluate、`inside + 1` 这类复合 safe-evaluate 表达式里的实际读取集合、条件表达式中 condition 和选中分支的实际读取、debug index-window base expression（例如 `evaluate("zr[1..3]")` 的 indexed-window result 保留 `global zr`），以及普通 postfix safe-evaluate 里的成功索引/成员读取（例如 `evaluate("zr[1]")` 报告 `global zr, index access`，成功 member 读取追加 `member <name>`）。短路 RHS、未选中的 `?:` branch 和 index-window bounds 只做语法/数值消费，不会因为其中出现可解析 identifier 就填充引用摘要；它仍是 adapter-facing runtime metadata，不是 parser-owned reference fact，也不声明 member declaration resolution。

Debug semantic-summary walker 现在会先按 AST 节点直接查询 `ZR_SEMANTIC_REFERENCE_WRITE` 和 `ZR_SEMANTIC_REFERENCE_MEMBER_WRITE`，再进入普通 read/member-access/position 查询。这样 `globalSeed = 3`、`seed.value = 3`、`seed[index] = 4` 这类 assignment 摘要不会因为同一节点或子节点还有 read/member-access fact 而丢失 write 事实；若普通 position 查询因优先级返回 member-access，walker 只对 identifier 节点使用 `ZrParser_SemanticFacts_FindReferenceAtPositionByKind(..., ZR_SEMANTIC_REFERENCE_READ)` 恢复同位置的 read fact，例如 `seed[index]` 中索引 token 的 `reference read index`。协议层仍只展示 parser 已写入 `SZrSemanticContext` 的事实，不在 Debug 层推断成员声明或写入语义。

## Fact Families

- `expressionFacts`: 表达式节点、源码范围、推断类型、精确度、常量值、调用目标 token、成员 token 和失败提示。
- `referenceFacts`: 声明和使用之间的符号关系、声明范围、当前到达定义范围、使用范围、引用类型和解析状态。
- `numericFacts`: 数值表达式的来源类型、目标类型、范围约束和潜在溢出状态。
- `reachabilityFacts`: 语句或表达式范围的可达状态，以及 return/throw/break/continue/常量条件等原因。
- `logicalFacts`: 常量布尔、数值常量比较、组合布尔表达式、恒真/恒假和短路推断结果。
- `ownershipFacts`: `%unique/%shared/%borrowed/%weak` 等所有权限定、生命周期区域、相关节点和违规状态。

## Lifecycle

`semantic.c` 仍然负责创建和销毁 `SZrSemanticContext`，但事实数组的细节由 `semantic_facts.c` 管理：

- `ZrParser_SemanticFacts_Init` 初始化六类 `SZrArray`。
- `ZrParser_SemanticFacts_Reset` 清空事实数组，并释放表达式事实里深拷贝的 `SZrInferredType`。
- `ZrParser_SemanticFacts_Free` 先 reset，再释放数组内存。

表达式事实追加时会深拷贝 `SZrInferredType`，并复制调用目标、成员名和诊断文本等字符串 payload。调用方可以释放自己的临时类型，事实层保留独立副本，避免 LSP 或 Debug 查询到悬空类型。

引用事实追加时会按 resolved declaration/write 的 `symbolId` 统一补齐自身 `definitionRange`，因此 parser/type inference 和 LSP semantic analyzer 的声明/写入事实共享同一个到达定义 payload 约定。

## Type Inference Emission

`type_inference_semantic_facts.c` 负责把 AST 节点和 `SZrInferredType` 转换为共享事实，避免继续扩大已经很大的 type inference orchestration 文件：

- `type_inference_constant_eval.c` 是同目录内的窄 helper，负责从 AST 证明整数字面量、浮点数值表达式、数值常量比较、logical-not 和组合 `&&` / `||` 的常量值。`type_inference_semantic_facts.c` 只消费这些结果来写 facts，避免把常量求值责任继续堆进事实发射文件。
- `type_inference_interval_logic.c` 是同目录内的窄 helper，负责从已有 integer `SZrSemanticNumericFact` range 证明简单比较恒真/恒假。它只在左右子表达式都已有整数区间且区间关系足够明确时写 `logicalFacts`；区间重叠、无 range、浮点或非数值事实保持 unknown。
- `type_inference_numeric_range.c` 是同目录内的窄 helper，负责 primitive numeric range、unary/binary numeric interval propagation，以及 checked int64 `+`/`-`/`*`/`/`/`%` 边界。`type_inference_semantic_facts.c` 只保留事实写入与常量/逻辑事实桥接，避免把区间运算继续堆进 1000 行级事实文件。
- `type_inference_array_diagnostics.c` 是同目录内的窄 helper，负责 fixed-size、finite-max 和 no-finite-upper array computed-index diagnostic expression facts。它为确定越界写 `array_index_out_of_bounds` error，为已知区间部分重叠但可能越界写 `array_index_may_be_out_of_bounds` warning，为 min-only/no finite-upper-bound 数组上的已知负向可能索引写 negative-only warning，为已知非整数索引写 `array_index_type_mismatch` error，并设置 expression fact 的 diagnostic code/severity payload；fixed-size 消息使用 `array size`，finite `arrayMaxSize` / `min==max` 消息使用 `array max size`，无有限上界的负向 warning 不带 size label。truly unknown/no-inferable-range 索引策略仍留给后续切片。
- `type_inference_branch_refinement.c` 是同目录内的窄 helper，负责 simple true/false-branch numeric interval refinement。`ZrParser_TypeInference_PushTrueBranchNumericRangeScope` 会为 `if (seed < 10)` 这类 identifier-vs-integer-literal 条件创建临时 child type environment，把 then 分支内的 `seed` 区间收窄为原区间与证明区间的交集；true branch 也支持 simple `==` 单点交集，例如 `seed == 10` 会把分支内 `seed` 收窄为 `10..10`。当 true branch 排除的 inequality literal 正好等于当前 interval min 或 max 时，也会把 `seed != 0` 这类 edge complement 表达为单一区间，例如 `0..255` 在 then 中收窄为 `1..255`。true branch 还支持 simple `&&` 条件交集，例如 `seed > 2 && seed < 10` 会按左、右比较依次堆叠临时 environment，把分支内 `seed` 收窄为 `3..9`。`ZrParser_TypeInference_PushFalseBranchNumericRangeScope` 会把 `<`/`<=`/`>`/`>=` 反向成互补边界后收窄 else 分支；当 false branch 排除的 equality literal 正好等于当前 interval min 或 max 时，也会把 `seed == 0` 这类 edge complement 表达为单一区间，例如 `0..255` 在 else 中收窄为 `1..255`。false branch 还支持 simple `||` 的德摩根互补交集，例如 `seed <= 2 || seed >= 10` 在 else 中会收窄为 `3..9`。两者都保留原 symbol/type/declaration payload，`ZrParser_TypeInference_PopBranchScope` 负责退出分支时恢复原 environment，并能释放组合条件创建的整条临时 environment 链。parser `ZR_AST_IF_EXPRESSION` 推断和 LSP semantic typecheck 共用这些入口，当前只声明 simple identifier/integer literal 比较的 true/false branch 收窄、true-branch equality 单点收窄、true/false-branch edge complement、true-branch simple `&&` 交集和 false-branch simple `||` 互补交集；interior complement 和 general inequality complement 仍不建模，因为当前 interval payload 不能表达带洞集合。
- `type_inference_record_expression_fact` 写入表达式 kind、源码范围、精确推断类型、值类别、字面量常量、调用目标 payload 和成员 payload。
- `type_inference_record_numeric_fact` 只为数值结果写入来源类型、目标类型、范围约束和溢出状态。
- `type_inference_record_expression_and_numeric_facts` 是表达式入口的组合 helper，并带按节点去重保护。它也会为 deterministic boolean/logical expression 写入 parser-owned `logicalFacts`，并为可证明短路的 skipped operand 写入 parser-owned `reachabilityFacts`。布尔常量求值现在会递归穿过数值常量比较、logical-not、以及可证明结果的 `&&` / `||`，让 REPL 和后续 Debug 查询不必依赖 LSP semantic analyzer 才能解释常量布尔、短路和 skipped-branch 可达性。
- `type_inference_record_primary_call_reference_fact` 在 overload resolution 成功后为 primary function call 写入 resolved `ZR_SEMANTIC_REFERENCE_CALL`。它复用 expression payload 的 callee-token 定位逻辑，但绑定到刚解析成功的具体 call node；事实携带 callee range、declaration range、function symbol/type id 和函数名。
- `type_inference_record_identifier_write_reference_fact` 为赋值左侧已解析 identifier 写入 `ZR_SEMANTIC_REFERENCE_WRITE`。assignment inference 直接从 type environment 读取绑定类型，保留 left identifier expression/numeric facts，但不再让左侧 token 走普通 identifier read-reference 路径。write fact 会把自己的 token range 作为当前定义 range。
- `type_inference_record_member_access_reference_fact` 为成功推断的成员读取写入 unresolved `ZR_SEMANTIC_REFERENCE_MEMBER_ACCESS`。`seed.value` 的 fact range 对准 `value`；`seed[index]` 的 computed member-access fact 使用完整 member expression range，并在写入前 materialize index expression facts。reference position query 先按更窄 range 选择事实，因此光标在 `index` token 上仍返回索引变量 read，光标在 `[` 或 wider member expression 范围内返回 member-access fact。
- `type_inference_record_member_write_reference_fact` 为非 identifier 赋值左值中的最后一个 member/index token 写入 unresolved `ZR_SEMANTIC_REFERENCE_MEMBER_WRITE`。`seed.value = 3` 的事实 range 对准 `value`，`seed[index] = 4` 的事实 range 对准 computed index 表达式；当前只声明 assignment-target token 分类，不声明成员声明解析。reference position query 会在同一 token 上优先返回 write/member-write，因此 `seed.value = 3` 不会被新增的 member-access fact 误报为读取。
- `type_inference_record_ownership_builtin_fact` 记录 `%borrow/%loan/%shared/%weak/%release/%detach` 这类 ownership builtin 的动作、结果 qualifier 和相关 operand 节点，让 REPL/LSP 可以读共享事实，而不是根据类型字符串重猜所有权语义。

当前已验证的发射范围：

- 整数字面量经 `ZrParser_ExpressionType_Infer` 后产生 `ZR_SEMANTIC_EXPRESSION_FACT_LITERAL` 和 `ZR_SEMANTIC_NUMERIC_FACT_LITERAL`。
- 已注册 identifier 经 `ZrParser_ExpressionType_Infer` 后产生 `ZR_SEMANTIC_EXPRESSION_FACT_IDENTIFIER`，并在类型带范围约束时写入 `ZR_SEMANTIC_NUMERIC_FACT_RANGE`。`seed` 注册为 exact `7..7` 后，identifier fact 与 numeric range fact 都会落在同一 token。
- 二元算术表达式经 `ZrParser_ExpressionType_Infer` 后产生 `ZR_SEMANTIC_EXPRESSION_FACT_BINARY` 和 `ZR_SEMANTIC_NUMERIC_FACT_PROMOTION`。
- `if (seed < 10) { seed + 1; } else { seed + 1; }` 这类 simple branch 在已有 `seed` integer range 时会通过临时 branch scope 收窄分支内 identifier range；`seed: u8` 或显式注册 `0..255` 时，then 分支内 `seed + 1` 会写入 `1..10` numeric range，else 分支内 `seed + 1` 会写入 `11..256` numeric range，LSP local semantic query 可读取同一 parser-owned numeric fact。`else if` 链、复合条件和跨块 numeric dataflow 仍保持后续任务。
- 复合表达式 AST 范围现在由左右子表达式范围合并得到，二元、逻辑、条件和赋值表达式都会覆盖 operator gap。`true || false` 的逻辑表达式范围覆盖 `0..13`，因此 `||` token 位置可以稳定命中整个逻辑表达式，而不是漂移到右侧字面量。
- `ZR_AST_LOGICAL_EXPRESSION` 现在通过 type inference 推断为 `bool`，成功出口会记录 `ZR_SEMANTIC_EXPRESSION_FACT_BINARY`、`ZR_SEMANTIC_VALUE_KIND_BOOL` 和 exact `bool` inferred type。parser/type inference 还会为 `true`、`false`、左右均为布尔常量的逻辑表达式，以及 `true || rhs`、`false && rhs` 这类确定短路表达式写入 `logicalFacts`。短路分析同时在 skipped operand 范围写入 `ZR_SEMANTIC_REACHABILITY_SHORT_CIRCUIT`，`causeNode` 指向证明短路的左操作数。非短路但结果已知的组合逻辑表达式，例如 `(1 < 2) && (3 < 4)`，会在完整 logical expression 范围写入 `ZR_SEMANTIC_LOGICAL_FACT_ALWAYS_TRUE` 并让 expression fact 携带 `hasConstant=true`。logical fact 与 expression fact 使用完整逻辑表达式范围，reachability fact 使用被跳过的右操作数范围，便于 LSP 在 operator/RHS 位置拿到类型和控制流解释，也让 REPL `:type true || false` 可以直接报告逻辑值、短路流和 skipped operand 不可达原因。
- 常量数值比较二元表达式现在也会在 type inference 成功出口记录 exact bool 常量和 parser-owned logical fact。`1 < 2` 的 expression fact 是 `ZR_SEMANTIC_EXPRESSION_FACT_BINARY`、exact `bool`、`hasConstant=true`、`constantValue=true`；同一表达式范围写入 `ZR_SEMANTIC_LOGICAL_FACT_ALWAYS_TRUE`。`3 <= 2` 对应 `ZR_SEMANTIC_LOGICAL_FACT_ALWAYS_FALSE`。这些比较结果也可作为外层 logical-not 或非短路逻辑表达式的布尔常量来源：`!(1 < 2)` 记录 false 常量，`(1 < 2) && (3 < 4)` 记录 true 常量。LSP local query 在比较或 `&&` operator token 上会返回 expression fact 和 logical fact，REPL `:type 1 < 2`、`:type !(1 < 2)` 和 `:type (1 < 2) && (3 < 4)` 会从同一 `SZrSemanticContext` 输出对应 `Logical value`，不执行表达式。
- `ZR_AST_UNARY_EXPRESSION` 的 logical-not `!` 现在对布尔常量 operand 写入 exact logical fact。`!true` 和 `!(1 < 2)` 都记录 `ZR_SEMANTIC_EXPRESSION_FACT_UNARY`、exact `bool` inferred type、`hasConstant=true`，并把 `relatedNode` 指向 operand。unary expression range 由 operator token 和 operand range 合并，`!true` 覆盖 `0..5`，所以 LSP local query 在 `!` token 位置会 materialize unary expression fact，而不是漂移到 `true` 字面量。
